<h2>All Reviews</h2>

<ol>
    <li> A Great Buy, Thank You.</li>
    <li> okay option for a 5 oclock shadow shaver. like the vaccuum feature... saves a lot of cleanup. battery lasts pretty well. buut razor usually takes 2&#x27;3 passes over a given area to get good consistent trimming. also difficult to get into nooks and crannies of a face such as between upper lip and note.</li>
    <li> This is a very good product and I would give it five stars without hesitation if the claim that it &amp;#34;does not make a mess while trimming&amp;#34; were true. The reality is that about 80% to 90% get sucked into the trimmer&#x27;s container, which is great, but it also means that the remaining 10% or 20% end up in your sink. Don&#x27;t get me wrong, I prefer this much over the alternative products that dump everything into your sink or next to it. If you use the trimmer with the turbo function, you get a decent suction and also a decent cut as long as you use the contour following comb. To get a good and even result, it is best to trim the same areas from at least 3 or 4 different directions, as the comb is not very fine and doesn&#x27;t catch all the hair. I have not had any problems with the hair container door -- other customers complained about it being flimsy but I find it easy to use and sturdy.&lt;br /&gt;The bottom line: This is a fantastic product, much better than all the other options. If Philips could bring themselves to drop the false advertising, I&#x27;d given it immediately five stars.</li>
    <li> Exactly as described and works as it should. Thanks!</li>
    <li> The quality you would expect.</li>
    <li> It is as promised and expected.  I&#x27;m happy.  Thank you.</li>
    <li> I bought it mainly for business trips (to avoid carrying the power cord) and the vacuum feature. Not even 20 uses and now the battery does not stay charged and the vacuum window stays open with hair flowing out of it.&lt;br /&gt;Kind of useless</li>
    <li> Great razor.  As most other posts say, this comes with the correct guide to make it work wonderfully.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I especially liked this because it had one head and the blade positioning adjusts.  This saves me from losing the 15 heads that most razors come with.</li>
    <li> Great product but ones you use it with water no longer works mind went out on me</li>

    <li> Ive owned several vacuum shavers and all worked pretty well. The Norelco seems to be the best of them all. I shave my beard very close to the skin and this shaver does a really good job. The vacuum is great as well and leaves no mess what so ever.</li>
    <li> Works well. Vacuum catches all the hair. No problems with theadjustable  length feature on the shaver.</li>
    <li> Pulls hair on normal speed, works perfectly on turbo (no pulled hairs). Blades are sharp and cut welll, but don&#x27;t use for fine detail or very close shaves. Vacuum feature is a gimmick - do not buy for that feature alone. The compartment fills up quickly and the overflow just sprays about your bathroom like mushroom spores. But I only bother shaving when I look truly overgrown so this may not be an issue for those who trim daily. Think of it more like a good ride-on mower as opposed to a lawn edger.</li>
    <li> Great product, excellent quality.&lt;br /&gt;Efficient seller.&lt;br /&gt;I recommend.</li>
    <li> I really like it. Just what I was looking for.</li>
    <li> ok....i spent a lot of time researching a beard trimmer and based on Amazon reviews chose this one.  This is just a hair trimmer and renamed a beard trimmer.  No difference except for a cheap plastic adjustable cutting guard.  I screwed up cutting my beard the first time with this.  So now I have the woman that cuts my hair trim my beard.  She does a better job and doesn&#x27;t charge much.  btw....she used a $300.00 3 inch trimmer to work on my beard.  You can&#x27;t go wrong buying this trimmer.  It doesn&#x27;t cost that much.  I still use it to do minor trimming.  Nice to have it around if i need it....</li>
    <li> The batery gone after one year. No cordless anymore</li>
    <li> This product is great! It does an outstanding job cutting and the vacuum catches all hair so my sink stays clean.  My only complaint is that I wish it was easier to clean. Since you cannot use water you need to use this very small brush to clean it every time. Just slightly annoying as it adds a few minutes to my morning routine.</li>
    <li> As a satisfied owner of a Norelco T980, I was pretty interested in the idea of a replacement trimmer that was quieter, lighter, offered better battery life, and wouldn&#x27;t have any battery memory issues (the T980 used Ni-Cad batteries). The QT4070 delivers in all of those areas. However, it suffers quite in a bit in an area where the T980 shined: quality.  I&#x27;ve had my T980 since 2008/2009 and while the battery isn&#x27;t very good these days, it still works perfectly. I purchased the QT4070 in September 2013 and Norelco is about to send me my FOURTH replacement under warranty. The first trimmer died completely after a couple months. It just wouldn&#x27;t turn on right after shutting it off, I couldn&#x27;t get it to show any signs of life on the charger either (I&#x27;m guessing the Li-Ion battery just failed). The other three have all succumb to the issue with the trimmings door others have shared here. The plastic notch that holds it shut is just too flimsy/fragile and breaks off after a few months of normal use. It&#x27;s a shame, because this is a nice trimmer overall and it just seems like a huge waste of resources. Philips could easily remedy this, but they probably consider it too minor of an issue to spend money on. Though, I do commend them on issuing replacements without any hassle whatsoever.  Minor Update - 7/5/2015: I should also mention, I&#x27;ve had a handful of instances where the battery just kind of &amp;#34;quits&amp;#34; when using the trimmer fresh off the charger. I usually have to stop to empty the trimmer and/or add/remove one of the combs after using it for a few minutes. Sometimes, it just refuses to turn back on and shows that the battery is dead. Very annoying.</li>
    <li> Had a Philips beard trimmer for 6 years and still have no issues with it. Decided to upgrade!</li>
    <li> Hard to trim mustache.</li>
    <li> Amazing, if you have a beard you need one. Best Trimmer on the market</li>
    <li> This trimmer is powerful, has great battery life and a good length selector. All of that would be enough to buy it.&lt;br /&gt;The vacuum feature though. Oh that sweet vacuum feature.&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m not saying it gets all of the hair, but easily 80% of the hair is sucked up into the little vacuum compartment.&lt;br /&gt;Your wife is tired of you leaving little beard hairs all over the sink, this helps with that. In a way, you&#x27;re getting this for the health of your marriage.&lt;br /&gt;Seriously though, this is a great trimmer, I would highly recommend it.</li>
    <li> This thing sucks. It is large and cumbersome to use. It does not give an even trim (left me looking like a mangy mutt after trimming my beard!). The &amp;#34;vacuum&amp;#34; attachment misses a lot of hair, so you still get hair everywhere. Lastly, does not allow for detailed sculpting without removing the guard completely, which is still hard to use due to the unhandy size. Eff this thing.. wish I had sent it back instead of hoping I would like it. I liked my $20 Whal much better. :P</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve had this trimmer since Dec 2011. Overall I have liked it. Though, recently the battery has had it. A full charge now only lasts a couple minutes. The upside is that the trimmer still functions while plugged in. Something my last trimmer wouldn&#x27;t do.</li>
    <li> Excellent. Perfect trimmer. Great battery, great use. The trimmer goes down to basically a 5 o&#x27;clock shadow. What more could I ask for?</li>
    <li> **Updated Review**&lt;br /&gt;Its now been about two years I guess.  Now in order to use the product I have to have it plugged in to start.  Otherwise Its says error and turns off.  If I plug it in and start using it I can unplug it and it continues to work.  But pretty annoying.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Should note, it will not catch 100% of the bear hair as you cut it.  But its gets a lot of it.&lt;br /&gt;Note sure if I would get the same one again, with how this is my second and now have this issue.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First one I got did not work, Amazon took it back and sent me a new one.  Second worked great and still does. Uses twice a week for months now.</li>
    <li> I bought this to replace a T980 Philips Norelco beard trimmer that was about 6 or 7 years old. This model is more powerful and has better controls. I think the battery is better, but its not fair to compare it against an old unit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Great news. Mine came with two combs. The one that was on the trimmer in the box is the one most people are complaining about. The other one is the contour following comb. Norelco must be listening.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The only feature I can complain about is the vacuum. It works and is okay, but it is not nearly as effective as the T980. The T980 had a spring-loaded lip this model doesn&#x27;t have. I am guessing it increased the suction on the T980. I would still buy this unit again, even over a new T980 if it was available. I always had to clean up a little hair afterwards and a bit more won&#x27;t make a big difference.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One note of caution. The door for the compartment holding cut hair protrudes a bit on the right hand side. At first I figured it opened on that side, but pulling it didn&#x27;t do anything. Be sure to open on the other side, I can see that a good pull on the wrong side could break the door.</li>
    <li> Update 2013-06-17:  Product was received in less than 2 days.  The contour comb was included and so far, impressed with the product.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Original Entry:&lt;br /&gt;Having read so much about the contour comb issue, I chatted with Philips-Norelco and got the following information.  I&#x27;m giving this 3 stars without even laying eyes on the product.  The chat was brief, to the point and satisfactory.  I will come back and update when I receive the product.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Mack: Hello Jim.&lt;br /&gt;Jim: Mack.. I&#x27;m interested in ordering a QT4070/41, but there is a bunch of complaints as to whether the unit comes with a contour comb. Your site shows one, but the manual doesn&#x27;t mention it. On Amazon, the same page shows that it has it and doesn&#x27;t have it. Make sense what I&#x27;m asking?&lt;br /&gt;Mack: I totally understand your concern and will be glad to help you.&lt;br /&gt;Mack: Jim, we have reported this issue and the new QT4070 now includes the contour comb.&lt;br /&gt;Mack: The contour comb is now included with the new QT4070 package.&lt;br /&gt;Jim: Do you think a new amazon order will include it, or would they have inventory dating back before it was included?&lt;br /&gt;Mack: Unfortunately, we do not have that information.&lt;br /&gt;Mack: Jim, you can purchase the unit. If you do not receive the contour following comb then you can contact us and we will replace it for you.&lt;br /&gt;Jim: Sounds good. Thanks.&lt;br /&gt;Mack: You&#x27;re welcome, Jim.&lt;br /&gt;Mack: Is there anything else that I can help you with today?&lt;br /&gt;Jim: Nope. You were very helpful and spot on. Thanks for the feedback.</li>
    <li> In the past I have almost exclusively used razors to shave.  This has been problematic since I would often get lazy and let my scruff grow out and then trying to shave would not be a pleasant experience.  I received the QT4070 today with a nice mantle of scruff today.  I took it out of the box, popped on the contour head, plugged it in, and was shaving away in just a couple of minutes.  It cut through my scruff with ease and the contour head did a great job of doing it evenly.  For those who have complained about the vacuum not working well I would imagine you had a fairly good beard when you did this.  My first pass left a fair bit of hair in the sink, but this is partially because I filled up the vacuum chamber quickly.  I emptied it and went for another pass with almost no hair flying around the bathroom.  The turbo setting makes this even handier.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, all in all, I would say get this product if you are looking for something that will leave you a little stubble and you are not wanting to do a detail trim.  Also, I wouldn&#x27;t worry about the alarming reviews cautioning about the potential to get cut with this product.  I zoomed it around my face on the 1mm setting without a nick or a scratch.  Just use it the way you are supposed to and you will be fine.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Buy it!  You&#x27;ll like it!</li>
    <li> Bought it on March 14th, 2015 and it has failed to hold a charge more than a few days at a time; it reads fully charged but the next day it is dead. Because it has been 33 days (3 days past the Amazon 30 day return period), I can&#x27;t return it to Amazon, so now I have to deal with Norelco. Shame I really like the features, it allows me to keep my beard neat and trimmed, and the vacuum works well. I can plug it in, and use it right away after it is dead, but if the battery is failing now, how long can it last? If Norelco is able to replace it with one that works as advertised, I will update this review  with a more favorable rating. But for now I cannot recommend this product.  Got off the phone with Norelco, and they are sending a replacement within 10 days, so I updated this from a 2 to 3 stars. If the replacement works well I will update this again.</li>
    <li> Trimming per say, i do not have any complaints about this product.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I hate to clean up the sink after the trimming so i purchased this product because  the concept of Vacuum Beard interested me. To some extent it really pulls the hair into vacuum chamber while trimming but not as much I expected, I still have to clean up the fallen hair. i guess I had high expectations.</li>
    <li> I bought this for my husbands bday. He has always wanted to have the &amp;#34;perfect stubble&amp;#34; look.. However he has not wanted to pay the price that some of the advertised trimmers cost loves all the options on the settings. He said he would buy the same one all over again. He was also impressed that it came with a charger. that was one feature he was a must. There are 18 secured length settings.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Turbo power boost increases the cutting and fan speed, and it contains a powerful lithium-ion battery, giving it a long life. It can be used with or without the cord. It also features a travel lock so that it won&#x27;t accidently get turned on when you&#x27;re traveling.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The razor comes with a two year warranty. This razor is the perfect indulgence for the man who wants a quick-charging mustache/beard/stubble trimmer.</li>
    <li> Compared to any other trimmer on the market, I venture to say this is the most superior.  I have owned at least 4 different types, including another Norelco.  By any comparison, this product exceeds my expectations and makes other trimmers look like garbage.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The trimmer is a pleasure to hold and seems ergonomically designed.  The build quality is very solid- to the point of impressive.  Adjusting the trimmer is accomplished via a rubber coated adjustment wheel that is accessible on both sides of the trimmer.  There are length indicators on the side vertically (a scale in inches) and the adjustment size displays on the LCD screen in millimeters.  This provides a precise cut to those who require such precision (not me).  The width of the blade area is more than sufficient for face and other areas (more on that later). Touted as a Vacuum trimmer, it does a pretty good job overall with some room for improvement as it may not vacuum all hair although that may depend on the length of hair being cut. Hair collects in a little compartment with a swing door.  The trimmer is rechargeable (a stand is not included however- just the charger).  Despite being rechargeable, the trimmer is very powerful, easily cutting through thick beard.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Some Issues&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As stated before,  the vacuum does a decent job, but not a great job at collecting hair.  The shorter the hair, the better the job.  At the very least, it seems to significantly contain the mess.  Another issue is that due to the design of the blade guard, you cannot really trim right up under the nose.  It gets pretty close, but not quite.  Finally, neither a beard brush, travel case, or recharger stand are included.  I was a little surprised in this regard.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am unable to comment at this time on how long the battery will last. I will have to edit my review after a few months to see how the charge stands up.</li>
    <li> My husband promptly \\&quot;handed down\\&quot; his old beard and mustache trimmer when I gave him this one.  He says it trims everything better than his old one and he loves the vacuum feature on this unit. The vacuum provides terrific ease of use and keeps everything neat and tidy.  The compartment is easy to empty.  The trimmer is easy to adjust with length measurements listed in both mm and increments of an inch as well as an LED number setting.     <li> My husband has a beard longer than the maximum trim length of this shaver, but, since he does cut his sideburns and shave his neck (or, rather, lets me do so), and since his 20-year old Norelco is getting very tired, I figured this was a good tool to try out for the job.    The shaver is very clean and sleek - it fits comfortably in the hand, has a cord that attaches to its bottom, not someplace inconvenient like a side (you can use it plugged in or not), and the controls are intuitive. My only objection to its form-factor is that the thing is LOUD. This is not so much because of the blades, however, as because of the powerful vacuum that sucks the hair into the cutting blade.    To change the cut depth, you rotate a thumb-friendly control that both physically raises and lowers the removable guard, and also lights up a large and easy-to-see LED readout that gives the depth in millimeters. (If it&#x27;s possible to change that to inches I never figured out how). The current depth setting is also indicated by two small rulers on the sides of the guard - right side metric, left side inches. For some bizarre reason the setting between 3/8 inch and 5/8 inch is \\&quot;15/32\\&quot;, not 4/8, and the longest depth is 23/32, not 6/8. I assume some engineer translated the millimeters into the closest inch measurement, and didn&#x27;t think about tolerances and usability.    I found that for very short whisker lengths this worked very well - it took off the hairs cleanly and quickly, with just a couple of strokes (I had to play with the orientation a bit - you need to stroke with the closed part of the guard forward, not the open side, or you&#x27;ll get choppy results). For longer lengths (taking sideburns from two inches to 23/32) I had to start off with a scissors and then use the shaver to even things out, which wasn&#x27;t worth it. The shaver also ignored hubby&#x27;s mustache completely, even on turbo, but the hair there is very stiff and lies flat, so it wasn&#x27;t cooperative about being sucked into the guard. I finally took the guard off and used the shaver freehand. I found the shaver to be quite easy to clean, using the included cleaning brush (I wish there was a way to attach this to the powercord, like a chuck key with a drill).    For short neat beards that get shaved regularly this is recommended. For longer ones that get trimmed once a month or so it&#x27;s a bit pricey, but still useful.</li>

    <li> I very rarely write reviews; but the Philips Norelco Qt4070 Turbo Vacuum Beard, Stubble and Moustach Trimmer Pro, Black/silver is certainly a PRO which needed reviewing.    I bought a Wahl as a back up in case the Phillips did not live up to my expectations.     All I can say is that the Wahl is now being gifted to someone.     The Phillips Norelco turned out to be close to perfect. I can honestly say I have never had a groomer that worked so perfect. Each hair the same length.     Now, there are flaws; but the flaws lay in the directions included with the product (or rather not included). Also, many reviewers before me seem to be selective readers.    1. The product does what it is suppose to do with no flaws. However, you can make it have flaws through usage. This goes with any product.    2. Yes, the guard can poke your lips as the tips are pointed (as posted by a reviewer). But, only if a person decides to use force/pressure. For example; you can have a needle to your skin and not feel it, but put force/pressure and you will. It is the same with the pointed guard (the guard is not sharp as a needle - I was just giving an example). It is designed not for use with force/pressure, instead let the machine glide and do the work.    3. For me the Philips Norelco Qt4070 is designed to do the work, by placing no force/pressure on the machine. I simply glide the Philips Norelco Qt4070 over my beard. The guard comb is flexible. It is designed to adapt to the chin area and curves on a face. Again, if you put force you will (IMO) have problems. Basically, if you choose a hair level and put force, the hair will be shorter than the level chosen. If you place no force, the hair will be the level you choose.    4. For those of us who have facial hair since we could grow it; we know that hair does not grow in one direction. It grows in many directions. So sometimes to get every hair the right length you need to find the angle/s that is/are right for you. For me, I find using themachine with the hair grain as oppose to against the hair grain works amazing. If I go against is is too short (for me).    5. The vacuum cleaning door does not close as securely as I would like it to close. It has open from time to time. But, a little tape in the corner helps.    6. Do not expect to find a product that does all you expect when it comes to facial grooming. No product will meet all your expectations. But, the Philips Norelco Qt4070 Turbo Vacuum Beard, sure does come close.</li>

Like anyone presented with the option, I went straight for turbo mode and never looked back, and so far haven&#x27;t seen any diminution of indicated battery power after half a dozen uses.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;According to the manual, you can use the trimmer when plugged in, even if the battery is dead, so you don&#x27;t have to wait for it to charge if you&#x27;ve drained the battery and you need a trim in a hurry - it will suspend battery charging while you use it off of AC power.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The included double-ended cleaning brush seems suited for the task of brushing out the screen in the vacuum debris chamber, but also looks as though it will be easy to lose.     <li> I&#x27;ve always been a fan of Norelco elctric razors since the early 80&#x27;s, so I had high hopes for the Philips Norelco Qt4070/41 Turbo Vacuum Beard, Stubble and Moustach Trimmer Pro. My hopes were not given over to disappointment, and I was met with a product that not only met, but exceeded my expectations. This trimmer can be used either corded or cordless, and for me, even on it&#x27;s normal setting, it does a fantastic job trimming hair, and keeping any trimmings cleany vacuumed into it unit&#x27;s storage compartment. I simply do not need turbo mode, though I admit I am not a person with thick or coarse hair growth. I can see Turbo mode being a handy feature for the hairier mammals of our species, however.     Battery charge life is long, and charge time is relatively short, around an hour from a dead battery to full charge, and numerous trimmings between charges. The LCD display shows battery level, as well as trim length setting, and there are length index marks along the side of the trimmer as well, a nice feature if the LCD ever goes on the fritz.     The size is easy to grip, not too small to feel awkward, and not to large to feel clumsy. In fact, it is a nice size to trim and neaten bearded areas other than the face, for those who are so inclined, without worry of clipper heads pinching any skin, they are well designed and simply do their job without risking any minor blood loss from the dreaded clipper bite other trimmers can give. While there is no mention of this practice in the accompanying literature, nor does Philips Norelco endorse or mention such use of this trimmer for that anywhere on their website that I can find, it is still a very capable tool that I have found fit for the job.    I was also surprised at how quiet and relatively minor the the vibration was of this trimmer, given how powerful and effective this little trimmer is. The trimmer comes with a little brush to clean it up with when you are finished using it, and for those who travel, there is a travel-lock that prevents the unit from accidently being bumped on during travel. Simply hold down the power button for a few seconds to lock and unlock this feature.    Overall a very rugged and well thought out device, worthy of anyones grooming arsenal.</li>

In my opinion, a precision trimmer isn&#x27;t too much to ask for considering the price and the issue with the contour comb (see Justin Yentile&#x27;s review). Aside from this, it&#x27;s still a great trimmer that gets all the hairs on my beard at a uniform length with barber-like results. I definitely do not regret purchasing the 4070!</li>

Going all the way down and then back up re-syncs the digital display with the actual setting.  Not a big deal since the setting is clearly marked on the side and the digital display is more just for fanciness.  It&#x27;s also rare to happen, but it does.</li>

For some weird reason the designers created an adjustable guard where the cutting blades actually stick out of the guard!   Yes - that big gap that you see on the picture means that the cutting blades can dig into your painstakingly grown beard in a flash, and you are left with the choice to trim it down (meaning a big change in your appearance) or hope nobody notices.     <li> First off--like other critical reviewers you&#x27;ll find here, I also had major problems with the comb. This review was almost a ONE-star rating, due to the sharp tines and general design of the comb. This _extremely_ poor comb design caused me to stab my lip several times and also resulted in uneven trimming.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Like other reviewers, I previously owned a Norelco T980 and needed to move \\&quot;up\\&quot; when it would no longer hold a charge. With the T980 no longer available, it appeared that my options were either the QT4050 or the QT4070. Overall, the QT4050 is far inferior to the QT4070 in that it lacks the travel lock, quick charge, and turbo functions. HOWEVER...the 4050 has one feature that I believe was SUPPOSED TO BE included with the 4070--the \\&quot;contour following comb\\&quot;. If you look closely at images of the two units side-by-side, you&#x27;ll see that the comb design on the 4050 is closed--no giant gap and sharp tines with which to cut/stab yourself--and it also has a flexible guide. Those who previously used the T980 will surely recognize the design!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In my frustration with the 4070&#x27;s comb, I did some research. Philips Norelco CLEARLY markets the 4070 as using their \\&quot;contour following comb\\&quot;. That&#x27;s not actually true for what&#x27;s \\&quot;in the box\\&quot;, however. The comb that comes on the shaver is model number 422203617701, which is their \\&quot;plastic stubble comb\\&quot;. As it turns out, the combs for the 4050 and the 4070 are _interchangeable_, and with a phone call to Philips, I was able to get them to provide the 4050&#x27;s comb--model number 422203617711.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After you get your shaver, if you&#x27;re experiencing similar issues with the comb, call Philips at 800.243.3050 and ask to speak with a supervisor--first level reps can&#x27;t seem to approve parts orders. Explain the situation, tell them you want the comb for the QT4050 (P/N 422203617711), and they&#x27;ll send it to you, free of charge. Within a week, you&#x27;ll be able to fully enjoy what Philips should have built in the first place!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For the record--after I received my new CONTOUR FOLLOWING COMB, the QT4070 is a FIVE-star trimmer--it&#x27;s exactly what I wanted. The one-star ding represents the hassle it took to get this product to be all it should be!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For the record--after I received my new CONTOUR FOLLOWING COMB, the QT4070 is a FIVE-star trimmer--it&#x27;s exactly what I wanted.     <li> I have read before that beard groomers which feature a vacuum are nothing more than a gimmick. They advertise themselves to eliminate those short, or long (depending on your beard), hairs that are the byproduct of any beard maintenance. The latter is directed towards those men who use manual means (beard scissors), or an electric trimmer without a vacuum. As far as this particular product is concerned: Philips Norelco Qt4070, I will be letting you know how it performs.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;APPEARANCE&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What we have first in appearance is a very modern, sleek looking accessory that has a blue digital readout. This is no old fashioned trimmer. Something that the girlfriend, or wife, would not complain (always a plus) about being in view for all to see. So yes, it looks good. Now that we got that out of the way lets get down to actually using it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Before you begin trimming, the manual notes that in order to perform the best job it is best to comb the beard out. But it does not come with a comb (my Remington did). This trimmer is certainly not one of the more inexpensive ones so why not have this included? Moreover, I can attest that combing the beard out definitely does help with a smoother, even trim. If you buy this product I would suggest buying one if you do not already have one.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;TRIM&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In order to determine the length that the trimmer will cut your hair, there is a MM and an inch chart on either side that will let you know what setting (i.e. 1 or 2 or 3 etc.) equals what. Personally I never get that involved with exact measurements when sculpting facial hair, but for the facial enthusiasts your need for preciseness will be satiated.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After I was finished doing the trim I came to two conclusions about this product: 1. It is impossible to trim under your nose and 2. The trimmings have to go somewhere, and seeing where they go, at least, might be better than not seeing. In the past I have not had any problems with other products in regards to the former, but the Qt4070 would not allow me to get anywhere on the upper lip.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There was still some mild shavings that found its way in my sink. It was not a couple, but it was not a lot either. It was enough to leave me thinking that the vacuum did indeed miss a few.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If this was the only problem I would concede to the vacuum and agree that it does improve the shaving experience. However there is one little thing that is neglected to be mentioned in the advertising that I was not aware of. As you may know, there is a vacuum that sucks up the hair and while it does not get every little hair, it does get the majority of it. Where does it go though?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Does it go in a little baggy that you can empty? No.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Does it go in a compartment that you can empty? Sort of.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Picture a bagless vacuum. Picture the compartment where all the hair and dust goes and forms that little puffy mass. Now imagine that after emptying the puffy mass, that you would now have to take the vacuum cleaner apart and clean every moving part within it because parts of that puffy mass had coated everything inside. Sound fun? It isn&#x27;t.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That is the experience with this vacuum groomer. After popping open the compartment, there is a wadded little mass of beard hair that simply falls out. Simple enough and quite fun actually. Though now you have to take off the measuring head to brush it and everything underneath. Ok well that is not so bad, right? But wait there&#x27;s more. You then have to slide up the little razors themselves to find hairs wedged in a not so neat compartment that was not meant to house little hairs. You will then find hairs all under and over the little mechanism that causes the blades to work in the first place (not the razors themselves--the part that moves them). Not to mention you cannot get all of the hairs out. This leads me to think that maybe this will lead to premature failure. This is all described in implicit black and white prints under the section \\&quot;Cleaning\\&quot;. Moreover, did I mention that the cleaning section has 17 steps? Yes, 17. And now we have reached why I have given it three stars.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This product looks goods, trims good (except for the upper lip), but I spent a good 10 minutes cleaning this after I was finished. Compare this to my non vacuum beard trimmer that leaves tons of hairs all over the sink. However, with the latter it only takes some water and a few hand splashes to get them to disappear. Time taken: 2 minutes and out the door. The vacuum is advertised to eliminate, or at least alleviate, cleaning just enough so that beard trimming can be spotless and trouble free (what else would it be good for?). Ironically, it causes more effort through the extra cleaning. Though the vacuum does work fair enough, it leaves much more to be done on my part which leads me to think it just might be a gimmick after all.cleaning section has 17 steps? Yes, 17. And now we have reached why I have given it three stars.     This product looks goods, trims good (except for the upper lip), but I spent a good 10 minutes cleaning this after I was finished.     <li> I try to maintain a short, stubble look, both on my head and my beard.  And this rather expensive option has turned out to be the most flawed of the dozen I have tried.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;PLUSES: The design is very handsome.  It&#x27;s easy to hold, the digital readout is nice, and the battery charge is certainly up for a lengthy trim job of hair, beard and body.  I&#x27;ve had models where the trim-length setting slips during use.  They have fixed that issue here.  However...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;MINUS: The plastic guides that run across the scalp, face and body are designed to serve two roles.  They direct hair into the row of blades for trimming, and the length at which they are set by the user should provide for an even trim.  They fail miserably at the second function.  The plastic guides are so flimsy, that with very little pressure, they collapse down, or spread from one another, allowing hair to get much closer to the cutting blades than intended.  The result can be as bad as rows of near-baldness in-between hairs of the intended length.  I have essentially had to shave my hair back to almost bald with no guard just to avoid looking like a freak.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This may work just fine for people with a 3/4\\&quot; beard or longer, but do not attempt to achieve an even, short look with this model.     <li> I have previously been using a Norelco T870 but the battery stopped holding a charge so I have had to buy a new trimmer. Although there were 3 reviews here that mentioned the guide being faulty I decided to try the trimmer due to the 20+ positive reviews and the lack of a decent alternative.   The trimmer arrived this evening so after charging it for an hour I tried it out.   The guide is adjustable to give a varying length of cut. The lowest setting gives a 2mm cut and the highest 18mm. Unfortunately, the guide is made using flexible prongs which bend a good 3-4mm. This means that if you use a low setting the guide prongs will bend fully to the blade. I found this out by cutting my lip twice in the first minute of use. I also quickly found that due to the flexibility of the guide using a low setting results in a really uneven cut.  I keep my beard pretty short (4-5mm) and there&#x27;s no way I can use this without the blade cutting me and without making my beard look like it&#x27;s been hacked at by someone with blunt kid scissors.     <li> I have had a beard, and thus have had beard trimmers, for almost 30 years, so I have some pretty strong ideas about what a trimmer should and should not do. IT SHOULD NOT STAB YOU IN THE FACE! But that is exactly what the new QT4070/41 does.    For years I was wonderfully happy with Norelco&#x27;s previous top-of-the-line model, the T980. I love the vacuum feature, the turbo setting cut my tough beard with gusto, and the length adjustment was generally adequate (though the settings were a bit wide apart, so 3 was too long and 2 was too short).    But the engineers at Norelco have taken a wonderfully designed T980 trimmer and screwed it up royally. The problem is with the guide comb. On the older T980, the guide comb completely covered the cutting head. But on the new Qt4070/41, the guide comb has tines that extend along the top and front of the cutting head, and END IN SHARP POINTS. So the cutting head sits exposed within a cavity between the ends of the two sets of pointy tines. Yeah, sure, that&#x27;s what I need to drag across my face all bleery-eyed in the morning - pointed sticks!  :-(    The new guide comb&#x27;s design is woefully stupid for two reasons:    1) The length to which your hairs are cut will VARY depending on the angle with which you hold the trimmer against your skin. If you hold the upper face of the guide comb flat against your skin, you get a longer cut than if you allow your skin to span the gap between the two set of tines. And frankly, you KNOW you can&#x27;t hold the trimmer at the same angle all over your face! BOTTOM LINE: AN UNEVEN TRIM!    2) Even if you are trying hard to keep the flat top of the guide comb flush against your face, you eventually have to turn a corner, like at your jaw line. I have used this Qt4070/41 about a dozen times now, and each time I have managed to jab myself with those stupid tines somewhere - in the jawline, in the chin, in the lip, etc. I know it&#x27;s just a matter of time before I (a) break a tine, or (b) draw blood. BOTTOM LINE: A PAINFUL TRIM    My advice: QUICK! Buy a T980 before it is discontinued and all bought up! Maybe Norelco will fix the Qt4070/41 by the time you wear out your T980.</li>

Now if you like to cut all this down to bare skin, then this shaver is 4 stars for you.     <li> Currently, this model by Philips and the Remington Touch trimmer are the state-of-the-art beard trimmers on the market. While the jury&#x27;s still out on the latter, given its very recent release date, the QT4050 &amp; 4070 lines have been out since 2009/10 respectively. I purchased the QT4070 recently and used it on a 4-week beard. The result was arguably the best trim I&#x27;ve ever had, owing to the innovative cutting design (flat head versus slanted, as with other trimmers), the consistency of the cutting, and the efficient motor, providing the torque needed to trim through a wiry undergrowth of facial hair (the turbo button is useful here). The vacuum feature works rather well, so that roughly 85% of the hairs were trapped in the receptacle beneath the cutting blades, obviating the need to use a towel or bowl under the sink to prevent drain clogging. The included brush suffices to clean miscellaneous hairs stuck to the blades (which conveniently require no oiling or other maintenance). Finally, the versatility of the trimmer, allowing up to 18mm of cutting length, puts it miles ahead of most brands on the market at department stores and pharmacies (Wahl, Conair, Braun, etc.). Conversely, Philips did produce a \\&quot;stubble\\&quot; beard trimmer that was woefully under-performing and cumbersome, so this line of trimmers is clearly an improvement. Overall, I&#x27;d rate the product a solid 9 out of 10. In future, perhaps a trimmer operating with lower noise emissions would round it out to a perfect score.</li>

I have sensitive skin, mind you, and not once has the trimmer nicked or cut it.  Not even close.  In fact, I am so confident of this Norelco that I bet I could have a Bloody Mary for breakfast before using it and still not hurt myself; I really have no idea how the gentleman who wrote the fearful review is going about using the trimmer.       When I purchased it, I was more interested in the trimming aspect; I had no interest in the vacuum feature.  That said, it works really well and makes no more noise than a typical electric razor.  It is easy to clean and quick to charge.  I use the trimmer every morning and charge it for one hour every 7 - 10 days.      A note on length.  Some say that you are left with a 5 o&#x27;clock shadow, but I have a very thick beard. At the shortest setting, I would say that my beard looks like it typically did not at 5 pm, but at 6 am the next morning.  Just a tad bit longer.  I suppose the effect will depend upon how thick your beard is, the color, etc.  At work no one even noticed that I had gone from a razor to a trimmer, so it is surely cutting closely.     In sum: after more than a month using this trimmer every day, I have had no nicks, no breakouts, and no worries.  Oddly, as one reviewer mentioned,your beard does feel different after trimming it each morning.  So go on: don&#x27;t fear the reaper.</li>

    <li> Review updated one year later, March 2015:  After 1 year of weekly use, I downgrade this to 2 stars. Durability for a Norelco product is very poor. Within 3 months (about 12 uses), the catch of the clippings door broke and I needed to keep the door closed with tape. Now after 1 year the hinges email of the door is broken so the door is taped both sides. About 4 months into using the product I thought it wasn&#x27;t holding a charge from week to week, which is strange because I use it maybe 10 minutes at a time and a charge should last 50 to 75 minutes of use. With trial and error I figured out that either there is a short or a loose connection triggered by disassembling the blade head to brush clean and or very mildly tapping to remove clippings. It doesn&#x27;t happen every time but the only way to make it work again is to put it back on the charger for a full charging period.  Original revieew March 2014:   Four stars because it includes the contour-following comb, which is more comfortable than the fixed comb which is attached when it arrives packaged. I paid for the upgrade features like 1-hour charging and two comb options, but now find I would have been OK with the features of the QT4050 because the 4050 has only the desirable contour-following comb but 8-hour charging. I&#x27;m going to keep this, but I wanted to let others know that if you don&#x27;t need fast-charging, get the lower model, and more importantly, in terms of comfort, the contour-following comb is better than the fixed comb. I had the G380 several years and the Ni-Cd batteries weren&#x27;t lasting very long, so a new trimmer was a must. I searched the reviews here on Amazon. What I really needed was a beard and mustache trimmer and that&#x27;s what I focused on. Also, it was time to go Li-ion technology for the improved charging and duration. The G380 was a combo system, meaning it included a nose-hair trimming head (hurts), a big comb to trim hair (never used), a smaller head for sideburn trimming (worthless) and a tiny foil head for &amp;#34;shaving&amp;#34; (again, worthless). If all you need is a beard trimmer, avoid combo kits as they don&#x27;t have good auxiliary tools. If you need one of those other tools, buy it separate.  To summarize, this is a good trimmer. Comfort should be your first priority. The contour-following comb is the more comfortable comb to use; the &amp;#34;fixed comb&amp;#34; sometimes grabbed my beard while trimming. Lower-cost models like the QT4050 have the better comb (per Amazon description), with a slower charger, but would be worth the savings.</li>

It worked at speed until the end, then asked for more juice.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I keep my beard and mustache close, never more than a quarter inch out.     <li> I&#x27;ve had a beard for 10 years-- the majority of which i&#x27;ve used a panasonic beard trimmer which wasn&#x27;t great but it did the job. This will require you to turn off the trimmer and empty the hair trap numerous times during each trim.  This has nearly tripled the time it takes me to trim (previous to the Norelco, I simply trimmed over the sink- problem solved)  5) This trimmer does not function when you attempt to use it upside down in an attempt to reach tight spots like the part of your mustache right underneath your nose.  This results in the sloppiest mustache trim I&#x27;ve ever had the privilege of wearing.I end up having to use scissors to try and clean up the areas this trimmer cannot handle.     In short-- if you don&#x27;t particularly care for small details and/or your beard is very long- this trimmer may work out fine.  But if you like a tighter beard with more detail, this trimmer cannot function at the most basic level.</li>

Comparatively poor battery life  The battery life leaves a lot to be desired since I&#x27;ve had a trimmer with a lithium ion battery. After returning this model I purchased the [[ASIN:B001GQ3GEY Wahl Lithium Ion All In One Trimmer]] I have charged it only once since purchasing it, i.e. in the past 12 months! So unless the spacer guide is non-removable on the QT4050, it should also go down to \\&quot;1/64\\&quot; of an inch. This kind of misleading marketing annoys me.     <li> Overall, I cannot recommend this trimmer based on several design flaws I believe will be problematic for most users.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The highlight of the QT4070 is probably its design \\&quot;look and feel\\&quot;. Since the vacuum opening is raised very close to the cutting blades (and is no longer a flexible shutter), it gets in the way of making straight line cuts. This is a critical issue that should be corrected for a trimmer at this price point. I would rather the vacuum feature work less effectively in order to have the trimmer work as expected - if a trade-off is required. Not being able to easily trim neat sideburns defeats the purpose.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The device itself also feels lighter, and has the feeling of less durability compared with earlier models. Likewise, the door is also a part of the storage volume, so when you open it up, shavings are likely to fall out and create a mess.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The digital blue cutting depth and charging indicators look very nice; however, the rotary length selector lacks grip and is not smooth to turn, i.e. it feels cheaply made.     <li> I&#x27;m probably one of the laziest people alive when it comes to beard grooming. I trim my beard because of a policy at work. Keeping that in mind, I quickly run over my beard once a week with this trimmer. And for the most part it does a decent job. It comes with 2 combs, one that contours to your face, and one that stabs you. Leave the second one in the box, it&#x27;s worthless. I usually get 3 trims out of the battery, which is cool, but pointless. When&#x27;s the last time you were in a bathroom with no outlet? The trimmer is adjustable for cut length, which is my favorite feature of this product. It adjusts in 1mm increments, and it tells you on the LED display what length you&#x27;re at. Pretty cool. Another cool thing about this trimmer is how easily it pops apart and snaps back together for cleaning. Now on to what is not so cool. The vacuum feature is a gimmick. It fills up immediately and sometimes to the point that hairs are backed up and blocking the trimmer blades from cutting. You have to stop and empty it, but yet there are still hairs all over my sink. So it really only catches some of the trimmed hairs. You&#x27;ll still have to clean up the sink and counter afterward. Personally, I&#x27;d rather skip the mid-trim emptying, and just let it all fall. The other thing I find lacking with this trimmer is the ability to edge. The blades are located in such a way that it&#x27;s difficult to get my upper lip, near my nostrils. I end up using scissors there, which does not go with my lazy beard grooming philosophy.  Update: Now I&#x27;ve had several months to use this trimmer. I&#x27;m reducing it from 3 stars down to 2 stars. The little door that holds the vacuumed hair no longer stays closed. The snap has broken, allowing the door to flap around if I don&#x27;t keep my thumb on it. And I still find it annoying that I have to empty it constantly during trims. Comparing this to my previous trimmer, a $10 Wahl Beard that lasted me over 5 years, this product is clearly not in it for the long haul. Piece ofjunk...and an expensive one at that.  Update 5/21/17: I&#x27;ve had this trimmer a few years now. About 6 months ago I noticed that the battery quit holding a charge. If I unplug it, the trimmer will only run a few seconds before turning off. It&#x27;s now a corded trimmer. Also, the springs inside the contouring comb always pop out when I remove it for cleaning. EVERY SINGLE TIME. The little plastic clips that hold the springs in place are no longer functional. This product has reached the end of it&#x27;s run with me. I did manage to get almost 3.5 years of use before calling it quits, but I wouldn&#x27;t say I was a happy customer during that time. I&#x27;ve ordered a corded Wahl Peanut to replace this trimmer. Something I probably should have done a long time ago, but I wanted to get my $50 out of this product. Funny, the Peanut sells for $40. So in summary, I really have no clue why this product has such a high user rating. I do wonder if most of the users rate it after a single use and never look back. Because really, and I mean REALLY, this trimmer was pretty much a huge letdown. I do not recommend it for any use for anyone. Here&#x27;s to hoping the Peanut works out much better than this...</li>

    <li> UPDATE TO THE BELOW...  After less than a year, the battery only lasts a couple minutes if lucky. The power cord plug easily slips out of the bottom (and could drop in sink of water if you&#x27;re not careful) as the plug doesn&#x27;t seat itself solidly into the body of the trimmer. And finally, The little plastic door you open to remove the hair from the trap had its clasp wear out after just a few months, so no it just flaps around loosely and spills hair everywhere unless you&#x27;re careful about holding it down. So, off the shelf, this is great, but it becomes a pain to use after a year. One fix for the cord is that you could super-glue it into the body of the trimmer since the battery won&#x27;t end up being practical after a year anyway, and then that solves the dangerous problem of the cord plug constantly falling out...but then you have to be near an outlet. At this point you might as well buy a $40 T-edger trimmer that will last you much longer.  This was a replacement item for a Panasonic ER-GS60-S trimmer that died after less than a year of use.  The Panasonic was great while it lasted (not quite as good as this one), but the battery not being able to hold a decent charge after less than a year is unacceptable.  I wish I had found this Norelco trimmer sooner as it functions slightly better than the Panasonic with its vacuum and because the guard locks in place with the turn of the dial (the Panasonic&#x27;s guard would get bumped out of place sometimes, although I think they also have a new model with a dial to fix that).  But I like that I can use this while plugged into the wall whereas the Panasonic was limited to operating after charging on the stand for a while.  It&#x27;s a little loud with the turbo mode on...louder than a regular pair of Wahl or Conair hair clippers, but not obnoxiously loud.  You may or may not wake someone sleeping with the bathroom door shut. Regular mode, you&#x27;re probably fine, but I always use Turbo for my beard. It doesn&#x27;t catch all the hairs with the vacuum, but I&#x27;d say it catches about 85-90% which still helps dramatically with cleanup. The hair-trap door swings outward, pivoting from a hinge that&#x27;s located on the right side...you have to give a slightly aggressive push and pull on the left side to swing it open.  If you buy straight from Norelco, it now ships directly with the contouring head that everyone is raving about in the comments (apparently they removed it on the original change from the older model, but they now give you both heads in the packaging) so rest assured, this comes with everything you need.  The head has the widest range of lengths I&#x27;ve seen on any unit so far, and allows you to adjust 1mm at a time which is nice. I use this for a short stubble trim all the way up to side-burn cleanup, so the range is very nice.  It&#x27;s also very safe for body grooming, so this really does it all.  I can&#x27;t think of anything I dislike...it could maybe use a slightly stronger vacuum, but that may increase bulk of the trimmer and decrease battery life, so I can&#x27;t really complain.  This fits nicely into my compact / travel shaving kit, so I like it just how it is.</li>

    <li> This trimmer is a definite step up from my older Norelco, which essentially had only the most basic feature of a trimmer:  An adjustable guide.  In the interest of deciding whether it&#x27;s worth it to spend the additional money, I will compare the two.    The QT4070 blade cuts very smoothly and evenly, much better than my old Norelco.  The old Norelco (without vacuum) had clippings all over the sink and counter--the QT4070 vacuum captures around 97%, which leaves the sink and counter pretty clean.  The QT4070 battery keeps its charge well.  The QT4070 digital readout ensures I have it set to the correct length, and lets me know how much battery power remains.    There is, however, the need to be more careful in the use of the QT4070 than my old Norelco.  The QT4070 has a gap between the top guard and the side guard, which leaves the cutting surface more exposed.  (I.e., you can stick your chin between the guards, and get closer to the trimmer than the guard setting would otherwise allow.)  On the old Norelco it was impossible to bring the cutting surface too close since the guard covered 100% of the cutting surface.  I was initially concerned, but got the hang of it by the second use.    Conclusion:  The QT4070 is of course a luxury, but it does deliver for the additional price.  Any trimmer will do the job.  For the additional cost, the QT4070 will provide a smoother and more even cut, with a much cleaner sink and counter, keeping its charge well, and providing a clear digital readout.</li>

This allows the skin at that point to be pushed closer to the trimmer depending on how hard it is being pushed into the skin. The door of the trimmings chamber has long since lost its latch (though it was repaired numerous times. All in all - as I an experienced user I say its official - this trimmer is a piece of crap that fails to fulfill its advertised promises of a measured length trim, maybe catching 50% of the cut beard, and apparently the trimmer is done when the battery is dead since the company provides no easy method of battery replacement.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Did a lot of research before I purchased this beard trimmer. What can I say I make a living researching things.  I always read the 1 star reviews first and look at the percentages of 1 star reviews. I have had the trimmer for about a month and used maybe five times. This trimmer seemed to be the best reviewed - with the least serious complaints.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Battery - The first charge for three hours and until the lights went out as instructed - had a run time of about five minutes before it was dead. I charged it again until the light went out and it that charged lasted through three ten minute trimmings and still had two bars. The battery now retains a full charge as described in the literature and reviews. Not charging the first time - gave me some trepidation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cutting - The shearing of the clipper even on regular speed is quite adequate for my beard. I haven&#x27;t used the turbo to trim with because for my beard it isn&#x27;t necessary. If the sound is an indication I could trim my hedge with it. The good news is the trimmer has yet to pull my beard - something other brands seems not to manage.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cutting guide/gauge - this part of beard trimmer designs seems to be universally lacking in all brands from my research. This trimmer adjusts well mechanically - but actually guiding and picking up the beard to cut it doesn&#x27;t function at all- probably narrower gaps between the trim guide comb teeth. My beard lays close to my face and I had to have at least two trims before I managed to get all the longer hairs caught and cut - so don&#x27;t do what the ad says and throw away your scissors - you&#x27;ll need them for a perfect trims. I did my first trim at 12 mm and it was the one with the most missed hairs - and a lot of post-trim scissor work. The second I did at 10 mm and that was more accurate in both length and catching errant hairs. My last trim was at 7 mm and that was the best yet. Caught nearly all of the beard. I think this was a result of both my personal beard anatomy, my getting used to the light motion required to cut evenly and I think the trimmer guide/gauge is probably is more accurately functional for shorter settings. In my beard&#x27;s case I have to go repeatedly in the opposite direction of the beard lay (and a lot of other angles) to get uniform cutting to the gauged length.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Trimmer Vacuum - Well... to me this is more of an advertising gimmick than it is an engineering/design success. My beard is light colored and I trimmed it last time with a dark tee shirt on. My estimate that less 50% of my trimmings made it into the trimmings vacuum receiving chamber - the rest was very plainly all over my dark shirt. Oh, and I suggest you wear glasses - I even got beard trimming thrown up in my eyes on occasions. I think the vacuum is great idea, but it will need a better intake design and far more suction before it is really functional.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Summary - I only give the trimmer a three star because its performance is a long way from being what is advertised and or perfect. That said, and based on reading hundreds of reviews on other brands of similar trimmers - this may be the best beard trimmer (at least for some beards) on the market today. I&#x27;m not sure that is good enough to please a lot of people. I will be keeping the trimmer - and my scissors.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update: Had and used the trimmerfor three months now. I am exceptionally frusturated with the trimmers inability to lift the beard to make accurate cutting. No matter how many times and directions I go over my beard - there are far too many un-cut hairs. Consequently, my beard varies from 8mm - the cut setting - to 20 to 30 mm. because the horribly designed comb simply does not function. My beard trimming now consist of ten minutes of mowing the beard with the trimmer from every conceivable direction - and then another 10 minutes using my comb and scissors to cut all of the beard to the same length. Bottom-line is this product is not market ready, nor does it perform as advertised. I have down graded my original review to two stars and that is generous.</li>

I think Philips realized that everyone wanted the original trim guard, so they just started including both. I honestly don&#x27;t know what the strange guard is even for (pictured here:[...]), since it doesn&#x27;t seem to work very smoothly no matter what way I used it.    If I wanted a trimmer to keep a couple millimeters of hair on my face, or to trim an existing beard, this might work alright. The vacuum was useful when I was testing it, but it got in the way more often than it helped on the low trim settings. The \\&quot;turbo\\&quot; feature was kinda cool, but I don&#x27;t see why it just wouldn&#x27;t always be on. Louder, I guess. I had it on pretty much all the time as I tried to trim as much as possible.    The last downside is the price. Sure, it has a lithium battery, but for 50 bucks? That puts it in the range of some rather fancy trimming devices. Worst part is that I paid more than that for it a couple months ago, only to (likely) never use it again. Maybe I&#x27;ll grow a beard or something.    I instead picked up the Qt4022:[[ASIN:B004QWST7Y Philips Norelco Qt4022/41 Stubble Trimmer Pro]]  This thing works fantastic, as advertised (actually does .5mm trim) to give you the permament 5 o&#x27;clock shadow look. It works great, and for less than half the price, I highly recommend it. It works while being plugged in and charged, and is waterproof. NiCd batteries last me about two weeks when I use it daily.</li>

    <li> Fans of the late lamented Norelco T980 vacuum beard trimmer will find a worthy replacement in the QT 4070, which does everything the T980 did and offers a better battery and illuminated display in the bargain.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For my money this is the best beard trimmer currently available for a number of reasons:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* The vacuum feature means no more beard whiskers in the sink. Once you have used a vacuum beard trimmer, you won&#x27;t want to go back to a trimmer without this useful feature.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* The contour comb and dialable length settings make it easy to trim your beard to a consistent length. (Yes, the 4070 now comes with the spring-loaded contour comb familiar to T980 owners; no calls to Philips customer service needed!)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* The 980 had a nickel cadmium battery, which cordless appliance owners know is subject to battery memory problems that decrease charge capacity over time. The 4070 has a lithium-ion battery that doesn&#x27;t share this problem. It also charges fully in just an hour.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* The illuminated display shows the trimmer length selected in millimeters, as well as the current battery charge.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* The power supply (which folks often refer to as \\&quot;the brick\\&quot;) is as lightweight and compact as any I&#x27;ve ever encountered, desirable attributes if you take the 4070 traveling.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The only negative I can report is that the 4070 really shouldn&#x27;t be called a stubble trimmer, as the closest trim using the contour comb is 1 mm. Guys looking for a real stubble trimmer might consider the Man Groomer Scruff Sculptor, which trims down to a third of a millimeter, but which also suffers from some unfortunate functional and ergonomic deficiencies.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The 4070 is a much more polished product than the Scruff Sculptor and represents a much better value as well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Perhaps the next generation of Norelco vacuum beard trimmers will trim closer. Until then the 4070 is the beard trimmer of choice.</li>

    <li> Like some other reviewers here, after 3-4 years my Norelco T980 quit holding a charge. The 7300 &amp;#34;feels&amp;#34; a lot more sturdy than the older model. Norelco appears to have spent so much time firming up the housing of the trimmer and adding a little LCD display (totally unnecessary), but they dropped the ball on the most important part of a VACUUM trimmer. The T980 caught around 95% of the hairs at 2 days to 1 week of growth, but the 7300 only catches about 80%. That may not seem like a big difference, and that&#x27;s probably why the product pre-testing made Norelco think this trimmer was fine... but when you&#x27;re in your own bathroom, an additional 15% of 1000 hairs is a lot of stubble to go searching around your granite countertop to clean up. I find myself spending about 3 times as long doing cleanup with the 7300 compared to the T980. The little cleaning brush they ship with it has also gotten a lot worse. Which is not too bad considering that you don&#x27;t need to open the door to remove trimmings, just hold it upside down and shake it a bit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;6 months later -- product rating 2/5&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The battery started showing wear. What started off as 1 week of use (10+ sessions) with a full charge ended up being two x 5 minute trimming sessions. Just charge after every use I guess, right?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;8 months later -- product rating 1/5&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The battery lasts 10 seconds -- so this is now my limited edition CORDED Philips Norelco QT4070 Trimmer&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall Thoughts&lt;br /&gt;I require products to last at least 1 year, with an expectation of two years.&lt;br /&gt;Perhaps I got a lemon, but considering some of the designs on this I dont think so.&lt;br /&gt;Many reviews on this site are probably from use within the first month or two.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My recommendation? Stick with Wahl&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My suggestion to manufacturers?  PLEASE produce non-throwaway products&lt;br /&gt;ie. replaceable batteries</li>

    <li> This trimmer has two uses, and excels at both. First, if you want the scruffy look, this is an easy way to get it and keep it. You can set the length of scruff you want (I use 3mm), and then just run this over your facial hair every three days or so. Takes way less time than traditional blade shaving, and you don&#x27;t have to do it every day.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Second, if you have too much length to easily shave with a blade (say, after a long, casual vacation), this trimmer can reduce the length down to something easily manageable with a blade. For that, I go all the way down to 1 mm. It is much faster and easier to do the two-phase approach (trimmer, then blade shave) than to try to make a five-blade razor chop through 1/4 to 1/2 inch facial hair. It&#x27;s worth having this device for that purpose alone, because it isn&#x27;t very expensive.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In either case, it&#x27;s easy to use. Just slowly brush it over the area you need trimmed. Some areas I find it helpful to approach from two directions, one after the other. The neck under the chin is an example.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You set length by twisting a dial, using finger and thumb. The dial goes through the device, and is exposed on both the front and back. An LED shows the length, and a scaled area on the sign does too. The LED is in millimeters, while the scaled area is in fractions of an inch.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A single charge works over a month for me. It recharges fairly fast.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One minor glitch: at one point when I was fumbling with the length adjustment, the dial slipped and then the trimmer would only go down to five millimeters. I had to force it all the way in the other direction to make it slip the other way, and then it was fine. Lesson from this is, don&#x27;t force that dial, and pay attention to what you&#x27;re doing.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve owned many trimmers, razors, and shavers and this one seems to be the best one out there. It seems with this trimmer that being afraid to make some minor mistake is not the way to go if you expect to have a nice even shave, and no you do not have to apply pressure, just let it trim the full length of hair up to your skin. So, with that being said, I will explain the pros and the cons:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:&lt;br /&gt;- Easily switching trimming lengths&lt;br /&gt;I have a goatee and a full beard so I tend to trim them both down to different sizes, so switching easily to different lengths was a big deal for me. This shaver does that with no problem, simply slide the adjuster and keep shaving.&lt;br /&gt;- Turbo mode&lt;br /&gt;I guess this is a pro, as the few times that I have used it I haven&#x27;t really noticed a huge improvement in the speed and efficiency of shaving seeing as the regular mode does the job just fine in a timely manor.&lt;br /&gt;- Battery life&lt;br /&gt;I charged it once I received it to full battery and haven&#x27;t charged it since and have been using it almost on a daily basis. (Have owned it for almost two months.)&lt;br /&gt;- Vacuum&lt;br /&gt;The vacuum is new to me. In general it&#x27;s great because before I had to deal with cleaning up a lot of hair in the sink and now the cleaning is very minimal. Depending on your beard size and how much you trim, you may have to do multiple empties of the hair trap.&lt;br /&gt;- Precision&lt;br /&gt;This is a major pro for me. If you use it correctly and know the right length to trim everything down to then this trimmer can be very accurate at giving you an even shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;- Vacuum&lt;br /&gt;The hole where the vaccum sucks in the air is somewhat small and can get clogged easily. If you&#x27;re letting your goatee/beard grow out and trim down a decent amount then expect to make many trips to clear out the hair trap and unclog the hole.&lt;br /&gt;- Sans Beard&lt;br /&gt;Obviously this is a trimmer and you can&#x27;t expect to be able to get a full clean shave out of it, but it gets it down to a fairly minimal amount of stubble to be able to easily shave it with a companion device. In hindsight, maybe I didn&#x27;t work at it enough to get a full clean shave as most of my shaves are early in the morning when i&#x27;m rushing out the door.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all, this is a great trimmer and I would recommend it to anyone who has a beard or goatee.     <li> Pros: It does what it&#x27;s supposed to do; it did arrive with the second (\\&quot;Contour\\&quot;) trim head; the trimming blades are wide&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons: Too many parts with flimsy construction; needs a small moustache comb; you are limited by few other similar products&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It appears from many, many previous reviews that this trimmer had arrived with only  \\&quot;Stubble\\&quot; trimmer\\&quot;, and not the \\&quot;Contour\\&quot; trimmer.  As is the case with several more recent reviews, my trimmer was thankfully packaged with both (in fact, this was the first thing that I checked).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I like the Norelco QT4070.  I got a good trim the first time I used it, as I was able to apply techniques learned from 10 years experience with the Wahl Trim-n-Vac (the only other trimmer I&#x27;ve ever used).  The Norelco arrived with the \\&quot;Stubble\\&quot; trimmer already attached.  I don&#x27;t use this trimmer since I can&#x27;t figure out how it&#x27;s supposed to work.  It has a large gap in the combs across the front of the trimmer blades, which just looks like a disaster waiting to happen.  I immediately removed it and attached the \\&quot;Contour\\&quot; head, which is what I always use now.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The instructions state that you should use a moustache comb (or any fine-toothed comb) in preparation before using the trimmer, very good advice which I certainly always follow.  It&#x27;s just that the trimmer doesn&#x27;t come with one.  For the 50 bucks people pay for this thing, one might think Norelco could throw a small moustache comb into the box (fortunately, I retained the one that did come with the Wahl Trim-n-Vac).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One very nice feature is that it can work with the cord - you don&#x27;t NEED to charge it.  It also does a very good job of vacuuming beard trimmings.  But one must remember: it will NOT catch every shard of trimmed hair - NO vacuum trimmer out there will!  You WILL still have to clean up afterwards.  Another nice feature is the wide trimming blades, which measure at least 1-1/4 inches.  The Wahl was only 1\\&quot; wide.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The problems I have are with flimsy parts.  First, as many reviewers have pointed out, the door holding the beard trimmings is very cheaply constructed.  Both the hinge and the small tab which keeps the door closed seem about to break at any moment.  A better design would be like the Wahl Trim-n-Vac, which used a removable cup to capture trimmings. No small pieces, no moving parts, no chance of failure.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Secondly, as many, MANY other reviewers have stated, the trim head combs are flexible and not rigid.  This means that someone can easily compress the comb, resulting in a trim SHORTER than that set on the unit!  Therefore, you MUST remember to be careful and NOT push too hard as you shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Third, the \\&quot;Contour\\&quot; head has a weird, overly-complicated design.  It has a flat top which is a separate piece that pivots on a spring-loaded hinge.  This is supposed to move in order to stay in contact with your skin as you move the trimmer around your face, chin and jaw.  As with the other parts I&#x27;ve mentioned, the spring feels very weak and seems prone to break.  A far better design would have been a trim head NOT with a flat, movable top, but with a single-piece, CURVED top, negating the need for moving parts to maintain contact...again, JUST LIKE the Wahl Trim-n-Vac.  I suggest Googling it for pics to see what I mean.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I am satisfied with the Norelco QT4070.  It does what it&#x27;s supposed to do, which is provide an even trim for my beard.  It does vacuum much of the trimmings.  It has wide trim blades.  It can be used with or without the cord.  But I have many concerns regarding parts that are at the same time cheap &amp; over-engineered.  And Norelco really should provide the 15 Cent moustache comb its own instructions recommend people use with this product.  Lastly, anyone looking for a vacuum beard trimmer will be hard-pressed for other options, as there just aren&#x27;t that many vacuum trimmers out there.  After doing a lot of web-research, I figuredI&#x27;d take a chance with this one.  So far, it does well, but I do hope this trimmer lasts even a fraction of the 10 years my Wahl Trim-n-Vac lasted.</li>

It is noisier than any of my previous Norelco trimmers too.  On the plus(?) side it uses lithium batteries so it goes full power until it stops unlike Nicad batteries which warn you by slowing down a little one or two shaves before stopping.  I hope this never stops dead when I am running late for an important appointment.  The regular speed and vacuum power is really more than enough, so I am wondering why they gave it a \\&quot;turbo boost\\&quot; setting.  I tested it out of curiosity and my ears actually hurt when I shaved near them.  I can&#x27;t imagine turning on turbo it in real life use.&lt;br /&gt;Update of 4/23/13&lt;br /&gt;I recently tried to see if the two \\&quot;blade heads\\&quot; on my last Norelco fit this razor and they did.  Using the old blades improved the experience significantly and one of the blades was a special blade for close fine trimming which was not part of this new razor.  While I am now happier I am not changing the rating since the improvements didn&#x27;t ship as part of this razor package.  The point is to recommend you see if any earlier Norelco blades you may have on an old razor will fit on this one.&lt;br /&gt;Update of 11/11/13&lt;br /&gt;The \\&quot;difficult door\\&quot; retaining the clippings (mentioned above) no longer works since the catch no longer holds it closed.  A little plastic nub disappeared and now it requires a rubber band around it tokeep clippings from being blown around the room...they need to rethink designs.</li>

    <li> As my older Norelco T980 finally started to show its wear after its remarkably long life, I decided to upgrade to its replacement top-of-the-line trimmer. After studying many wildly-mixed reviews, I had some concerns with the newer razor. However, considering how happy I had been with the performance of the T980, and my intended use of the trimmer for achieving stubble, I dismissed the negative reviews about trimming longer hair and purchased the trimmer anyway. Initial impressions were very good.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The QT4070 looks very sleek. It feels much ligher than the T980 while offering a seemingly larger hair chamber and the LCD display, which deserves its obligatory mention. It&#x27;s ability to use both corded and cordless is also an excellent feature; my battery arrived drained, but plugging it in allowed immediate use. It also does away with the spring-loaded vacuum \\&quot;chute\\&quot; that forever frustrated my use of the T980; it replaces it instead with a solid-plastic chute that extends all the way to the clippers. Unfortunately, my excitement was curtailed when repeated uses of the trimmer all left hair covering the counter top. I&#x27;m not sure if the defectiveness is due to this change, or a new, weaker vacuum.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My trimmer arrived with both of the described heads - a fixed \\&quot;stubble\\&quot; head, and a spring-loaded \\&quot;comb\\&quot; similar to the T980. The stubble head differs from the comb in two main ways: it has no spring-loaded tail; instead resembling a single, flat, solid unit atop the trimmer; and it has the \\&quot;guard\\&quot; teeth in front of the razors removed. The latter point seems to be a huge design flaw, leaving the razors entirely exposed and ultimately shearing skin twice in the first use before I resigned to using the \\&quot;comb\\&quot; head. The comb head, while much safer, also seems to perform poorly. Both the comb and the guard teeth seem much flimsier than the older T980, allowing the distance between the skin and the razors to vary depending on the pressure applied. This seems likeanother major design flaw, as it&#x27;s extremely difficult to hold the razor at the same angle, with the same pressure all over the face. The result is needing to re-trim areas of my face several times in a futile attempt to achieve consistency before ultimately accepting the uneven trim.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m left with the impression that the QT4070 is trying really, really hard to distinguish itself from the older T980. While the trimmer makes several significant steps forward in design; it falters on functionality, offering inferior performance with its vacuum and dangerous or uneven trims with the stubble and comb heads. If these issues were resolved, the trimmer would easily warrant a 5-star review. Unfortunately, in its current incarnation, I must reluctantly retire its use and return to my worn-out T980.</li>
    <li> I returned this product after trying it for a week because the vacuum is kinda gimmicky.     <li> I&#x27;ve had a beard for a long time and I generally get a new trimmer every 3 years. At least, that&#x27;s been the average life of the trimmers  I&#x27;ve had. I bought this Phillips Vacuum trimmer after reading reviews online and determining which would suit me best. My previous trimmer was a Wahl Lithium battery unit, which I was quite fond of but bit the dust after 3 years. Most of my comparison will be to the Wahl.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Good.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The thing I like best about this Phillips trimmers is its design and ergonomics. It has the same tactile rubbery plastic that my Phillips Sonicare toothbrush has, though with a black face for masculinity. It fits well in my hand and feels substantial and well made.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I also really like the adjustable length guide and the digital display. My biggest downside with my previous trimmer was that I had over a dozen attachments to keep track of. Also unlike my old razor, this Phillips does not require oil. It trims my beard very well and its easy to dial in the perfect length. Previously, Id trim on the short side and let it grow in. Not so with this trimmer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The big selling point of this trimmer is obviously the vacuum. It does work very well. I&#x27;d say it traps about 70% of the trimmings and the rest land in the sink. You would need to empty the chamber multiple times if you&#x27;re doing serious trimming duty, as it is pretty small. The vacuum is ideal for the lady friend because girls hate hair in the sink. At least that&#x27;s been my experience.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Bad.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My most prominent difficulty with this trimmer is that it is quite imprecise for edging. Because the vacuum surrounds the blades, it&#x27;s difficult to see where you&#x27;re going. I&#x27;m getting used to it, but my previous trimmer was much better.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The trimmer also lacks power compared to my previous one. I always use &#x27;turbo mode&#x27; because regular just doesn&#x27;t have the speed and vacuum power that is necessary.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In addition to edging difficultiesand lack of power, the blades are much larger than previous trimmers I&#x27;ve had. This means that its difficult to get close on cheeks and for neck shaving. It gets it down to a fine stubble, but for a smooth neck you&#x27;ll need an additional razor. Luckily, stubble is in fashion. So, i just let it be.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Finally, the battery is good for about two weeks with daily use. My Wahl went about 6 months on its first charge and it was much more powerful. The Phillips redeems itself by having the fastest charging time I&#x27;ve seen with a digital display of battery life. I charge it with a similar cycle to my Sonicare. The downside of the low life is that I have bring the charger with me if I travel, and a travel case was not included.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Verdict.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I love this trimmer. If they can address the issues I pointed out, it&#x27;ll be perfect. It&#x27;s great for beard trimming but bad for edging and neck shaving. I&#x27;m getting used to it and can tolerate its shortcomings because it does everything else so well.</li>
